This book is completed for you, O sons, who are studying this science of medicine in its entirety. I have reached the goal in it, made clear and explained its details. I find it fitting to complete it for you with this treatise, which is part of the practical application of the hand.
The practice of surgery in our land and time is almost forgotten, except that it should be studied and its effect felt. The only remains of it are simple drawings in the old books, their meanings and benefits obscured by errors and distortions until they have lost significance and utility.
I intend to revive and enrich it with this treatise through explanation, clarification, conciseness, and providing illustrations of the various tools used in surgery as an addition to the information and as a necessity for those who require it.
The reason there is no skilled craftsman in our time is because the art of medicine requires long study, and it is necessary for the practitioner to acquire a thorough knowledge of anatomy as described by Galenus before that. Until he becomes familiar with the functions, parts, and connections of all organs, their openings and closures, the bones, joints, muscles, their number and locations, their vessels and nerves, and the positions of their openings.
"Therefore, Abul Qasim says that physicians are many in name, but few in deed, and especially so in the craft of surgery. We have previously mentioned this aspect within the introduction of this book.
"For he who is not well-versed in the matters we have discussed about surgery, will not likely avoid making a fatal mistake as you have seen many do in this science who practice it with ignorance and negligence.
"That is why I saw an ignorant physician slice open a camel's hump on a woman's neck, intending to treat some of her ailments with incisions at the neck. However, he cut through a major vein, causing her to bleed profusely until she died between his hands.
"I also saw another physician who attempted to extract a stone from a man's bladder, as the stone was large and decayed. He broke it into pieces using a piece of glass. "The man died within three days, and I was called to extract the stone again. Upon examination, I found the fragment of the bone from the stone and the surrounding tissue, which showed that he could not have done it.
"I also saw another physician who earned his living by practicing medicine among the rulers of our land.
Al-Tibbi (the physician) hastened towards Suqas Ibn Mukarram, as he had a fracture near the elbow with an injury. He quickly set the fracture onto the wound in a strong and precise manner without leaving space for air to enter.
Then he released it (the fractured bone) from its fixation, then left him for some days and ordered him not to move his arm until it swelled, brought it out and cured the ulcer.
He called him (the patient) and hastened to remove the fixation, so he regained his comfort and became independent from his pain, except that corruption had already dominated the limb and I was unable to amputate it.
The corruption continued to strive in the limb until it perished.
I saw another physician with a protruding and swollen tumor, so he waited for days until the bone of its owner became soft, as it was a sarcoma (cancer) that should not be exposed to iron tools.
except it is in a limb that may require amputation entirely.
Therefore, my sons, it is important for you to know that work with hands has two types: a type of work that accompanies safety and another type of work that comes with pain in most cases.
"Be cautious in every place where this work requires fear and hesitation, you should avoid and reject it.
"Lest the ignorant find a way to speak and slander, take precautions for yourselves with armor and clothing, and treat your patients with kindness and firmness.
"Employ the best route that leads to safety and a praiseworthy outcome, and diagnose dangerous and difficult diseases.
"Be aware of yourselves against what you fear may mislead you in your religion and worldly life, for it will remain with the ignorant and raise you in this world and the hereafter to the extent of your abilities.
"Galenus said in some of his maxims: Do not treat a bad disease to be called good doctors.
"This article has been divided into three sections.
"First Chapter
"In the kiln with fire and in the kiln with sharp medicine, organized from head to foot, images of tools, hands with every tool needed for work.
"Second Chapter
"In fractures, dislocations, surgery, setting bones, and similar things, organized and images of tools.
The Third Chapter.
In Algebra, the removal of stones, and treatment of fistulas, and similar things, arranged from head to foot, with illustrations of tools.
The First Chapter.
On Veins.
Before we describe the work with it, it is necessary to mention its benefits, disadvantages, and in what temperament it is used.
I say that the discussion about the benefits and disadvantages of veins is a long, precise, secret knowledge that many sages have spoken about it.
They have differed in it and I have abbreviated their speech out of fear of prolongation.
I say that veins are beneficial in general for all ill temperaments, whether they are without matter or with matter, and these are the hot temperament without matter and the cold temperament without matter.
As for the cold temperament with matter, they have differed in it. Some said that veins are beneficial for it, while others disagreed and said that veins do not help in a disease of heat and cold because the nature of fire is hot and cold.
It is a possibility that it can be cured from hot and cold disease with a warm or cool vein, and the one who says otherwise states that veins in fire may help from a hot and cold disease in humans. Whenever you place your hand in a human body and moisten it to the state of fire, you will freeze the human body with cold.
And I say, by his words, for experiment has revealed this to me more than once, except that it is not fitting but for one who has trained and practiced in the art of incision with a sharp scalpel. And there is variation in the temperaments of people and states of illness within themselves, their causes and symptoms, and duration of time.
As for other diseases, there is no fear of them for you, and especially not for cold or wet diseases; for all physicians agree on this, and do not differ in the benefit of incision in them.
And know, O sons, that the secret of treating with fire and its superiority over medicine is because fire, in isolation, does not harm the part it touches or affect another connected part except for a gentle injury.
The medicine with fire may reach beyond the parts and perhaps create diseases that complicate the organ's pathways and even kill; but because of its nobility and dignity, fire does not do this except by excessive use.
It has become clear to us through experience that this is for the duration of service and care in craftsmanship, and standing on the truth of matters.
In this book, I have refrained from lengthy discourse, yet if it were not contrary to my book, I would have given you in the fire a secret deeply hidden and its method of performing it on bodies for expelling diseases through a philosophical explanation that clearly demonstrates understanding.
Know, O sons, that they have differed regarding the time which heals the eye and considered spring as the best time.
I say, the eye can heal in every time because the damage that occurred before the time will take a while to benefit from the eye. It is certainly the case that if the eye injuries are serious and irreversible, it cannot afford delay due to fear of aggravation; for internal damage caused before time may be greater than the external harm after time.
It does not occur to you, O sons, that the common people and the ignorance of physicians think that an eye which relieves from a disease should not return again and they make it forbidden.
The substance you refer to is not just a medicine that alters the temperament, but it also dries up the humors which are the cause of diseases.
The substance you refer to excels over the medicine in speed of effectiveness, strength of action, and severity of rule.
The disease may return at certain times depending on the nature of the causative factor, and it may be strengthened and worsened in the body by the gathering of substances within it and the body's preoccupation with acquiring them from food and similar causes.
May Allah not cause the disease that this substance is used for to be a severe or complex one, in a part of the body with a lot of substances and humors. Like the toothache, its cause can be prevented from returning and it may be less severe.
And as for the common opinion that this substance is the last resort in medicine, it is correct to some extent because they believe that there is no remedy that can be helpful with a medicine or without one after the occurrence of the disease and the use of this substance and the act of applying it differs from that.
The meaning of "this substance is the last resort in medicine" is that we use various remedies for a disease and they do not work, then we use this substance which succeeds; from here it becomes clear that this substance is the last resort in medicine. On the meaning that has become popular, and many doctors are ignorant about it.
The early people have mentioned that gold (al-kayy) is better than iron, and they said this because of the refinement and nobility of gold; however, it does not cause corrosion (mudqiqah), and this is not a general rule (ala 'l-italaq).
Because I have found that it is true only in some abdomens, not all; gold (al-kayy) is better and superior to iron as they said, except if you want to protect the container in fire, then the redness of the gold will not indicate for you the degree of heat you desire.
Because it heats up quickly and if you increase its heat in the fire, it melts quickly; thus, the maker from this is prone to error. That is why gold (al-kayy) with us is slower and further away from being suitable for work, if God wills it.
This chapter (Baab) is organized in the Kunya (gold) from head to foot, so that it facilitates what the student wants from it, if God wills it.
The first section.
In the head-Kunya, there is one Kunya.
This instrument is beneficial for the pressure and swelling on both skulls, which are causes of headache, frequent fallings from the head to the sides of the eyes and ears, excessive sleep and toothaches and abscesses of the shaving (area). For every disease that is due to swelling, such as pain in the testicles (falaj), headache, sciatica and similar diseases.
This image instructs the physician firstly to use a simple and easy-to-apply medication for the head for three or four nights according to the strength, habit, and custom of the patient.
Then, he commands him to shave his head with the razor, then he sits him between your hands with his hands placed on his chest.
Then, you place the tip of your thumb between his nostrils until the middle finger is reached, teaching this position by guidance.
Then, he squeezes the lemon-oil bottle which is shown in this image.
Expose from the bone the size of the nut or the size of a chestnut, then lift your hand and with it take the same iron or another one if it is rusty. Until you see what I have told you in the bone, then take something from salt and dissolve it in water, drink a little of it and place it at the mentioned position and leave it for three days.
Then, apply a linen bandage soaked in oil and leave it until the dryness disappears from the fire, then treat it with four-fingered frankincense until it heals, if God wills.
It is said that when a wound remains open, it attracts pus which is better and more beneficial.
Some of them mentioned that the skin should be sewn to the bone, and the sutures should be held until some of the marrow of the bone burns, then it is scraped away what has burned from the bone afterwards, and then treated.
Others said it is necessary to make the incision deep until it affects the bone strongly, so that a piece of bone falls off like scalp or small flakes, and they claimed that this leaves an opening in the skull and keeps the wound open for a long time.
Then it is treated until it heals, and I do not see any of these two types (of treatments) except in some people and on the path of recklessness and leaving it with me is better and safer because the skull contracts when its natural connection is severed as we have seen in other parts.
And it is not correct when the skull of an infant is weak by nature and the first type (of treatments) agrees with me, I prefer it and its use is recommended if God wills.
Chapter Two.
On the subject of the head also.
If a tumor occurs in the head, prolonged and it is not relieved by incision, lancing, cautery or caustic, or pressure bandage or leeches, and if one keyhole has been made but it did not relieve, then look into it again. If the head of the tumor is strong in structure and not weak, and it has a severe cold sensation, then make another keyhole slightly above it. Then make a keyhole on each side of the head until the pus is drained and the tumor is exposed from the bone that we have described. Make a keyhole in the posterior part of the head where it is known as the nape, and press gently in this place without breaking the bone, for the tumor will have severe pain contrasting with the pain of other keyholes on the head, and I shall specify this keyhole in its location.
The keyhole that is made in the side of the head and at its posterior part should be shallower than the one that is made in the middle of the head, as illustrated here.
Chapter Three.
In case of a fracture that is not displaced.
If a fracture of the skull occurs with swelling and it extends to the eye, empty the pus with appropriate medications for the head as described in the section on diseases, if this does not help, then treat it with trepanation from two sides. Either by burning medication or by iron (tool).
As for trepanation with burning medication, it is to take a clove of garlic, sharpen its sides from both ends, then drill the location of the wound with a wide needle until it reaches a space beneath the skin that can hold the garlic clove.
Then it is to insert it under the skin until it disappears, then tighten a ligature firmly around it for about ten hours, then dissolve (the ligature) and remove the garlic clove and leave the wound for two or three days before dressing it.
Cover it with an ointment made of oil until the area heals, then treat it with a hot poultice made of mustard until it is cured (by God's will), or you can do this with some burning medications mentioned in the 14th chapter on burning medications.
Regarding the cauterization with iron, it should be as follows: The bowl (should be) like this shape: [Picture/Image].
The iron bowl is named because its head resembles a bolt, having some knob at the center of it.
Then, place it (the iron) on the wound location and hold your hand, while slightly moving the iron piece here and there. The burning capacity should be similar to half of its length. Lift your hand (slightly) so as not to burn the surrounding flesh, which is below it, and then drink a poultice made of linen soaked in brine water and place it on the wound site for three days. Then, apply oil to the poultice and treat it with alum until it heals, if God wills.
If you wish, use a narrow knife-like notch from the bowl to make cuts in it for avoiding cutting of the surrounding flesh specifically.
Chapter Four.
Treating incisions.
If treatment of the incision is made as described in our previous discussion and no improvement is observed, check if the treatment mentioned in the list of diseases does not apply to it, or if one of the methods described earlier such as burning or application of medicine has not been performed. The mortar (makwaat al-sakeeniyya) should be cauterized until it turns white, after learning its position by a line of the length of half a finger or similar, and leaving your hand once, then pressing it until the veins are cut and approaching the bone.
You should be careful not to burn the connection between the jawbone and the moving muscle that it contains, causing inflammation.
Be aware and cautious of bleeding veins when you have cut them, as there is danger in the cut. Avoid, without doubt, anyone who does not know what he is doing and has no experience in the matter, leaving work to them.
Here is the method for treating bleeding veins on a face, if God wills: If you see a suitable method that this procedure does not achieve, do not use it.
You see a possible patient with an injury in the middle of the head, as we described previously, and treat the wound until it heals, if God wills.
If you wish to use the method we described in the chapter on cauterizing veins, it is better and more effective than this one.
Fifth Chapter.
Wounds of the Ears.
If a wound occurs in the ear due to cold and is relieved by easy treatment, and other treatment mentioned in the division has not helped, and the wound does not heal, then cauterize the hole that is called "the point," which is its image.
Then, it is cauterized around the entire ear or both ears in a circular motion if the wound is in them. Afterward, the distance should be increased slightly from the root of the ear after the location has been determined by measurement, and the distance should be about ten points in each ear or around it. Then, the locations are treated until it heals if God wills.
Sixth Chapter.
Fractures.
The fracture that is treated by the knife should only be of the type that occurs from a blow as described in the division of diseases.
A knife should avoid the type that occurs from dislocation and numbness of the nerves.
When this type of fracture is treated by the saws, files, and chisels and it does not heal, then the cause should be cauterized with three knives. One should be near the root of the ear, the second slightly below its base, and the third at the meeting point of the eyes.
Make an incision opposite the affected side as strangulation only occurs on the visible side.
The image of the incision should be made by making an incision opposite the upper ear, slightly below the occiput (back of the head), and on the other side in the neck, with a length equal to the width of the thumb.
Descend with your hand until you burn half the thickness of the skin, and this is the image of the cup or one type of cautery, which was presented only to be a little less rough as you can see. The cautery should have a slight sliver of gold, then treat the place as previously described until it heals, if God wills.
Section Seven.
Incision for a stopped-up nose.
If a nose is stopped-up and treated as previously described but does not improve and there is no cause for suspicion, make four incisions. Make an incision on each side of the head, one in the middle of the head as previously described and one in the nape of the neck at the appropriate place.
The description of the cups, and it may also be made an incision on the mouth of the nose to be deep, then treat accordingly.
Chapter Eight.
On the topic of amputation.
In cases of tumors, it is preferable to administer a strong laxative beforehand to cleanse the intestines and the brain.
Then, he should shave his head completely and on the second day, apply the plaster made of kohl as described in the article on fractures, several times, because it is a strong painkiller.
And perform the procedure on the indicated location, because if he has a seizure while doing so or if he does not, it will be necessary to insert three plasters from top of the head to the neck.
Place a finger between each plaster, then treat the tumor as described, if he wishes to increase the number of plasters and the patient is likely to tolerate it, apply the central one.
If he wishes to increase, apply the plasters on both sides and treat him until he recovers, and the plasters should be oily as shown in the image that follows.
Chapter Nine.
On the topic of the scrotum and swelling of the entire body.
It is necessary to first clean the head with laxatives as previously mentioned, then shave the patient's head and apply a plaster in the center of the head and one on each side of the head and another on his neck.
Three on the neck veins, if it (the disease) necessitates stretching the body more than that and the patient is likely to have it, and the disease is strong and decisive, then four ligatures on his chest veins. Reach with the cauterizing iron until it burns more of the skin and then lift your hand, then treat it as described until he recovers, God willing, and the cautery be zitouniya (olive-oil based).
The Tenth Chapter.
Incision of the Gland.
The incision that is performed on the gland, which precedes the abscess, should first be cleaned with large syringes and all the treatment mentioned in the section if the cause is severe and it is likely to take medication.
If it is a child who does not tolerate medication, do not use the cautery or the ligature for cleansing the head before that for several days with improving his diet.
Then shave his head, then make one incision in the middle of the head as described, and another incision at a later time. On each side of his head, if the patient is strong and it is likely that he will tolerate it, make the incisions as described on the abscess and stretch the body on the neck and chest veins, and the cautery be zitouniya (olive-oil based) as described.
If the patient is a child, make the incision gentle on this form.
The First Chapter [is about] Making an Incision Gently on this Form if the Patient is a Child.
On Operating Anuswerts (Patients with Rectal Prolapse).
If the cause of anuswerts (Rectal Prolapse) is excessive and hardened exudates, then use the vessels which we have mentioned in the owner of the penis [male genitalia].
If the cause of anuswerts (Rectal Prolapse) is discharge moving towards blackness, and the patient's body is soft, clean his head with what purifies it as it comes in the division [operation].
Then cut off the patient's head, then make a firm ball from cattail like a circle, and lower it into his center [anus]. The patient remains sitting upright, holding on to all sides, then take one hot coal from the fire of camel dung.
Then heat it moderately in the fire until it is as hot as a finger can bear, then empty it and insert it into the circle [anus] at its center. Leave it there until it cools down. Perform this procedure on the patient every week with his good treatment until he recovers, if Allah wills it.
If you want to cauterize it with many small points without holding the incision, let there be a smoky vapor. This type of cauterization makes the head [of the patient] sweat moderately.
Then lay a cotton on it (the wound) soaked in oil or raw chicken fat.
The second chapter is titled "The Second Chapter".
In case of water discharge in the eye.
If it becomes clear to you that there is water discharge in the eye with the signs mentioned in the section, then, clean the affected person's head and hair thoroughly from all moisture and wash his face in hot water in the bath house for a few days.
Then shave his head and clip the hair in the middle of the forehead, then clip two more on both temples if there is water discharge from both eyes or from one eye only.
Then cut with scissors all the hairs and veins that are under the skin so that the cotton swabs can be long enough to reach the temples and avoid bleeding.
If you see any swelling or inflammation, cut it at the spot with whatever treatment is available to you, and wisdom in healing the veins and cutting them off will be sought, along with avoiding bleeding.
There are two cotton swabs under the eyebrows.
The third chapter is titled "The Third Chapter".
In case of constant tearing (of the eyes).
If the eyelids are constantly stuck together and they were previously burns or scalds that are on the surface of the head from outside the head, and you think it is a thick cold ulcer with a bad odor, apply the remedy you have described at the beginning of hot water. A lesion in the middle of the forehead, two lesions on the eyebrows and two lesions under the eyes just below the bones. If it requires more, apply a lesion on each side of the eye on the eyelid with a small cup.
Fourth Section.
In the nose cavity.
If treated with what was mentioned in the section and the treatment does not work, force the suspect to swallow three hot peppers then shave his head and apply the central lesion with a cup of olive oil. Then apply with a flat iron (or metal cup) two times on the eyebrows, slightly under the hair and preserve the scalds, do not cut them, this is an image of the flat iron.
Fifth Ten Section.
In the protrusion of the eyelid.
If the eyelid protrudes due to a disease or swelling, apply a lesion with this crescent-shaped cup.
If you wish, make two incisions slightly above the eyelids on each side, and keep them away from the edges of the eyelashes, and let each incision be as long as the eyelid.
Do not stretch the skin too much, but only to the extent that a third of it is burned, and the appearance of the cup should be like this.
The Sixteenth Chapter.
In an Eye Cup.
If you turn them inside, the eye will be pushed out and the cup will be in it in two types. Either the cup is burned or the cup is with burning medicine, if it is burned then order the patient to leave the incision before that until it grows and becomes flat.
If it (the incision) is made near the plant, it (the wound) will shrink to avoid movement until it grows back. When it grows back and stops, place the head of the leech on your stone (pestle). Then learn (from it) on the eyelid with the cautery, as a mark in the form of a leaf.
The marking begins by drawing close to the incision, then a moist cotton is placed under the eyelid either in white or blue ink. After that, the image of this cup is imprinted on it.
Then gradually, the image is imprinted little by little in many repetitions until it burns the surface of the skin, which is shaped like a leaf of an aspen tree clearly and leaves a mark indicating the success of your work that you see the eyelid becoming swollen and the hair rising above the meat of the eye.
Lift your hand when that happens and leave it for three days, then apply cotton soaked in oil until the scab falls off, then treat it with mercury until it heals if Allah wills. If anything of the hair returns after a time and the eyelid swells again.
Prepare the eye again in that place as you did first, if there is hair in the lower eyelid, pull it out until it returns to its natural position and does not cause any hair loss from the eye. As for the cautery with medicine, it means ordering the leech to leave the incision until it grows and heals.
Then, make a figure of parchment resembling an ass, then take from the well-boiled soap and unslaked lime from each, weighing a dirham or similar, crush them altogether into a good paste and perform this with a pestle so that it does not harden. Then, spread it over the parchment that you have made resembling an ass's figure and place it on one or two eyes, then put a cotton soaked in white of egg and garlic beneath the eye.
Place your thumb on the medicine and press it gently, and move it whenever you feel the garlic, so that the medicine finds its way like fire, until the garlic no longer perspires, then leave the medicine and move it with your thumb, if the garlic subsides, remove the medicine, and wash the eye with water.
Observe, if you see the eye has swelled up as it does during burning or cutting, otherwise repeat the treatment in the place where the medicine had no effect and did not darken until your work is complete and the eye is healed, then put cotton soaked in oil on top of it to extinguish the burn.
Then treat it with the Nux-vomica (naghleh) or similar until it opens, and you should strive to preserve while working that nothing of the medicine falls into the eye. If the lid is adhered after days and there is hair in the eye, something should be removed from the eye.
Prepare the medicine specifically for this situation where the lid has adhered, as you did first, then treat it until it opens. This is a page of the horse's hide.
Know that human eyes can vary in smallness and largeness, so adjust your treatment accordingly. It is not hidden that there is a remedy for those who have this condition with this craft.
The Seventh Chapter.
Treatment for the nasal ulcer that appears in the corner of the eye.
If the nasal ulcer is treated with what we have mentioned in the articles on diseases and it did not heal, then you should try this feature.
The guilty person is ordered to place his head in your stone and a servant will hold his head between your hands so that he does not move or shake his head.
Then place a cotton swab dipped in egg white or in the ointment of the Persian roses on his eyes, then cover the container which is shown here.
Make it tubular, like the beak of an eagle, from one side which contains the cavity, and if you wish, from the other side. If you wish, it may be closed like a bladder, except that this form is best for your work, God willing.
Then, grind the nose if it is open and extract its contents and blow air through it or if it is not open, then open it and extract pus. Afterwards, place a cupping glass over it as it is very protective. Hold onto it until you reach the bone.
Move your hand slightly away from the cavity towards the nose tip to avoid mistakes or harming the eye, so that the cupping glass falls into the corner of the eye and corrupts it. If you reach the bone with the first incision, do not repeat the process unless necessary.
Leave it for three days, then apply a poultice with oil and treat it with warm oil until it heals. If it does not heal within 40 days, apply the sharp purgative medicine to reveal the bone and move it as will be described in its relevant chapter, God willing.
The last part of one of the Nasurs is mentioned at the beginning by some, he heads towards the Nasur (the nose) and breaks it then puts fine gravel inside its fracture (the broken nose).
Pour in it a measure of lead filings (lead shot) weighing dirhams, grasp the forceps firmly and tightly wrapped with a tampon soaked in white or water. The patient's eye should not move lest the corrosive lead is directed into his eye. It is necessary to place a cotton swab over the patient's eye.
If the lead burns the nasal passage and causes a strange stench, then it is necessary to use the incision in the nose (nasotomy) and redirect the nose into the nasal passages as appropriate for its condition.
The Twelfth Chapter.
On Fractures of the Eye.
Fractures of the Eye occur frequently, especially in children's eyes, and it is common for them to happen. If this fracture is treated as described in the classification section, treatment may not be successful. In such a case, a small cylindrical socket made of bone (a bone cavity) should be made on this shape.
The cavity should be on the handle of the scalpel, then place it in a pincer with a screw, inside the crack, until the knife reaches the depth of the crack, then treat it with cautery until it bleeds, if God wills.
The ninth section.
In the case of a nasal bone fracture in the mouth.
If it appears in the nose, or the nasal passage, or at the base of the nasal bones and a fracture occurs and bursts, causing drainage of blood from the nose, and treatment is applied but does not heal, then a cup should be placed over the fractured area to prevent infection.
Then, a pincer is inserted into the nasal fracture and the hand is held until the iron band covering it reaches the edge and end of the fracture, then this should be done once or twice, after which it is treated as previously described until it bleeds, if God wills.
If the tissue is cut and bleeds, there is no need for further examination. However, if it does not bleed, then examination of the site is necessary and the decaying bone should be removed as much as possible, if God wills.
The one hundredth section.
In the case of a deviated nasal passage or deformed nasal bone.
If the tooth abscess occurs due to moisture and the roots move, and you treat it with medicines but it doesn't improve, place a small stone on your palm then extract the cavity after that, placing the tube on the root.
Insert a tube, which is held with pliers, into the cavity and keep your hand slightly until the tooth feels hot as it reaches the root of the tooth, then raise your hand. Repeat this process as desired, then the tooth will fill with salt water.
Hold it for an hour and shoot at it, so the moving tooth will become fixed and the abscess tooth will harden and the corrupt moisture will dry up.
Chapter one, forty.
In case of toothache.
If the toothache is due to cold or there is swelling and treatment with medicines does not improve, then fumigate it using either hot oil or fire.
As for fumigation with oil, take beef tallow and heat it in an iron pot or a container, then take a small cloth and wring it on the edge of the container, dip it in the heated tallow and place it on the painful tooth using pliers and hold it until it cools.
Then, repeatedly heat it until the strength of the fire reaches the root of the tooth. If you wish to apply a swab or lint dipped in cold oil, place it on the affected tooth and cover it with the protected iron [instrument] until the fire reaches the tooth socket.
To use fire, it is to take a brass or iron pipe and fill it with some charcoal so that the heat of the fire does not reach the affected mouth, then heat the vessel whose shape resembles the tooth and place it on the same tooth and hold your hand until the vessel cools, do this several times.
The pain goes away either in the same day or on a later day, and it is advisable when using this method to fill the affected mouth with good oil and hold it for an hour then squeeze it, this is the shape of the vessel.
Tie it with any side you wish and to the thread that can be, this is the shape of the pipe.
The second chapter and the tenth.
In the operation of dogs.
If the dog is suffering from worms and cold dampness, and it has not reacted to drugs and you wish to perform a quick operation, then heat the hollow vessel whose shape resembles an outlet on both sides.
The excerpt should read: "The gas escapes from the cavity of the other side and it is placed as a pouch on the same worm again, if necessary, until reaching the depth of the worm. If the worm is small, make the tube according to the size of the worm.
Leave it for three days, then wrap it in cotton soaked in oil until what has been burned goes away, then treat it with balm and ointment until it heals, if Allah wills.
The third and fortieth chapter.
In the cavity of hoarseness of voice and shortness of breath.

Chapter Fifty-One.
On Cancer.
If the cancer is in its beginning and you wish to stop it, confine it with a circular band around it, as it rotates; some of the wise have said that it should be confined with a broad knife in the middle, but I do not see this because I expect it to break out, and I have seen that happen several times.

Chapter Two and Fifty-Six.
In the Matter of Bleeding.
The Matter of Bleeding: It is a corruption that consumes the body, as fire consumes dry wood; if you see bleeding in a place where there is possibility of burning, wrap many layers of small and large bandages accordingly for that place where bleeding occurs.
Then, apply it from all sides until the corruption is completely destroyed and nothing remains of it, then leave it for three days and apply large layers of quicklime mixed with oil on the bandages until all the dryness and all the corruption is cured.
Then, treat it with growing flesh for meat; if after three days you see that the meat is growing healthily without any corruption in it, then proceed to cauterize what remains of the corrupted places, as the bleeding can also be treated with caustic medicines.
It is faster to apply heat with fire; I have previously mentioned its treatment with caustic medicines in the division, so take it whenever necessary from there.
Chapter Three and Fifty-Six.
In the Matter of Straight and Bent Needles.
Often occurs in the soles of the feet this condition, it is a hard lump that afflicts the man, and it may be one of two types: either burning (Kiyy) with fire or cutting (Kiyy) with sharp water.
As for the Kiyy with fire, it is to heat a curved metal instrument similar to an eagle's beak made of iron and adjustable from all sides and thin at the edge. Then lower it on the nail and move your hand around the nail until the instrument reaches the depth of the nail.
And it remains for three days with pain, then tighten it with a sharp, rough pincer made of salt and leave the pinching on it overnight as it will dissolve from its roots. Then treat the wound with raw lard until it heals, if the nails are not crooked.
Often occurs on the surface of the body, particularly in the hands and feet. It is necessary to take a cannula made of copper or iron or an eagle's beak and place it on the nail or wart, then pour boiling water into the cannula as much as possible.
Your hand should be grasped and it should be rotated slightly with your thumb so that the pressure affects the anus in the center of the ligature, and the hot water will find its way to the center of the ligature. The patient should bear the pain of the hot water for an hour.
Leave it thus, the ligature will dissolve from its roots. Treat each area in this manner until it reaches all parts of the body. Then treat the affected areas after it has dissolved with cauterization using caustic agents such as lye.
The fourth and fifth sections.
For the paralytics.
If paralysis due to a fever or other causes occurs in a person, it is necessary to tie four or five knots on the back between each row of knots and one on the chest. And a knot with a bayberry kernel on his person, as paralytics find relief and speed in the recovery of cold diseases.
The fifth and sixth sections.
For the treatment of abscesses in the body.
If an abscess occurs in the body made of hard, rotten and harmful materials, it is necessary to tie a soft knot on each abscess with a goat's foot that has been heated over a fire or long zarand, or with a fig kernel.
The fractures occur initially in this state, they do not increase and the active principle of healing is agitated by it, except that it should be after the relief of the cause by cutting.
The sixth and fiftieth [chapter or section].
On the case of the dislocations occurring upon severing the ligaments.
Frequently, the dislocation of blood from ligaments occurs due to injury that exposes it from outside or due to fracture or wound or similar cases, and it becomes difficult to cut it.
If this happens to someone, hurry with your hand to the ligament area and place your thumb on it and press firmly until the blood is trapped under your thumb and nothing comes out of it, then put small and large, numerous clay vessels with olive oil in it and blow on them until they become very hot.
Then take one, either small or large, according to the wound and the place where the artery is cut and the vein descends on the same limb. After you have amputated your finger with a saw, hold the vessel until the blood stops flowing.
If the artery is cut during the amputation of your finger, and the vessel descends, take another vessel with the saw from the vessels prepared in the fire, and continue to do so one after the other until the blood stops flowing.
And keep a spare vessel nearby in case there is a need for another, and know that if the artery releases blood, it cannot be stopped unless it is one of the four ways: either by pressing (with a finger) as we have mentioned, or by applying a tourniquet if it has not yet swollen. If the artery is torn and blood flows, tie it with strong and secure threads or apply medicines that are known to stop bleeding and cause severe constriction.
And whoever tries to stop it with ropes or excessive pressure, or by applying hot objects and similar things, it will not stop the bleeding except in extreme cases. If someone is shown any of these and there is no doctor or medicine present, they should place a splint on the wound as we have described.
He should press it strongly until the blood congeals and coagulates from above the wound and on the arteries and veins, and he does not release it with cold water. The extreme cold should always be applied to it, until the blood thickens, hardens, and breaks, and during this time one must observe what requires it of any drug or substance.
Chapter Two.
On cuts, wounds, amputations and similar matters.
As we have mentioned in the first chapter, every disease is cured with fire and burning medicines, their causes and instruments, and the shapes of bandages, and we made this a comprehensive guide from head to foot.
In this chapter, I will present that method clearly to make it easy for the student to understand.
Before I begin with that, it is important for you to understand that this chapter contains more subtle matters than what was discussed in the first chapter on fire and burning medicines.
Due to this, caution is required because the work in this chapter often involves the loss of blood, which sustains life when an artery or vein is cut or injured due to a wound, puncture, incision, operation, or similar matters, all of which are accompanied by great fear and danger, and death occurs frequently in many of them.
I advise you regarding what contains ambiguity among you; indeed, it may occur to you in this craft, people with various ailments, from whom one may have injured by his disease and death approaches him.
I advise you regarding what causes pain and length of the wound, and the approaching of death by his disease, which indicates death. From them are those who spend their wealth for you in hope of health and cure of his disease, but do not aid you from one who is cowardly.
Be cautious of your eagerness and beware of that which is not certain, do not proceed with anything except after clear evidence that it leads to the praised outcome. Use knowledge and caution in all treatment of your diseases, and always consider safety.
Indeed, in this there is a means to gain praise and glory, rememberance and admiration. May Allah guide you and grant you success, for that is in His hand, there is no deity but Him.
This chapter has been expanded on the subject of the calf from the neck to the foot, so as to clarify for you what is intended by it, if Allah wills.

Chapter Two.
Section of cutting the two veins behind the well-known ears (temporal veins).

Before cutting them, the head of the patient should be shaved with a razor, then the place should be scratched strongly to make the veins appear, then the back of the patient's head should be pressed with a thick cloth, then look for where the pulsation is and their two lowered locations behind the ears, which are not visible except in some people.
Then press them with a tourniquet and cut them, cutting deep to the bone, this should be done at the head level, and if you wish, introduce the tourniquet from below the veins and tighten it upward with the cut being about two closed fingers in length.
If the artery is cut, blood will flow out in a pulsating manner towards the face and damp clothes, if the vein does not appear to be felt, it is necessary to probe from the ear at a distance of three fingers, then press with a tourniquet and press deeply to the bone.
Send vessels from the blood on the median part, and maybe send more or less from it, all of this according to the degree of weakness of the patient and his condition; then observe the wound. If it remains attached to the bone from the puncture, cut it off.

The Tenth Chapter.
Treatment of Severe Chill in Orbital Fistula of the Eye.
Often in fistula, something resembling chill occurs due to its severity and hardness.

If so, it will move to all sides easily. It should then be broken open with a force parallel to its width.
Then, I shall make an incision from all sides, extending until it clears out, then attach it to the scrotum and cut it, but if it does not agree (with you), do not cut it except after performing the amputation of the member. In that case, there is no harm in it. If the wound is large, gather it with sutures and treat it until it heals completely.
If the wound is small, there is no problem with it. The worms will naturally force themselves out and bite. After performing amputation of the member, it causes no harm. Then, wash the eye with salty water after cutting the abscess and treat the location with what bites until it heals completely.
The Tenth Chapter.
Treatment of the worm infestation that occurs in the scrotum of the eye.
The worm (sand fly) is a parasite found in the upper layers of the scrotum, and it often affects children. It causes heaviness in their eyes and makes them sensitive to sunlight during the day, making it difficult for them to see clearly. To make the eye run water.
To make the eye laugh (cry). Put their faces on permanent surfaces and let them sleep on it, making their eyes wet under the eyelids with moisture or applying snakeroot oil. When the situation is set with your fingers, feel for the snakeroot between them. The method is to place the patient's head on a stone.

Then, with the long blade of a scalpel, make an incision on the snakeroot in the length direction but not wider than the width. As for depth, make sure to cut the skin all the way down to the snakeroot.
In most cases, the snakeroot will emerge from the incision like a piece of white cheese. Use forceps that you have previously wrapped with your fingers to grasp and pull it outwards. Control your hand movements so that it comes out entirely and be careful not to widen the incision too much to avoid injuring the eye.

Chapter 10.

The second section:
To raise the ingrown hair from the eye with a lancet.
If there is hair or two hairs involved in the process, take a sharp lancet and insert a thin cotton thread made of fine, soft silk. Then tie the ends together to form a very delicate knot. The length of the thread should be about half an inch.
Then place another thin thread on top of the first one, tie their ends if desired, and position the patient's head on a hard surface near the sun to improve visibility since this is precise work. Next, insert the lancet with the thread into the ingrown hair root.
Insert the lancet into the eyelid until it exits from above the natural hair, then draw the thread to the surface and insert the thread back into the eyelid, if there is one or two or three hairs.
Then pull the eyelid with it until the ingrown hair along with the thread exits from the eyelid together with the natural hair. If you have pulled the thread but the ingrown hair has not come out with it, pull the thread back down to the upper hole until the thread exits from the upper hole.
Then let the hair grow in it, and gather them together. Do this until they rise to the top of the wound and can be seen by the eye. When that happens, excise the activity and the thread, then sew up the eye and leave it sutured for a few days or three, so that the hair remains in place and flesh grows on it.
If the hair is short, then either add long natural hair to it so that they both grow together, or leave it as it is for a while until it grows longer. When it has grown enough, lift it up.
The Third Chapter.
Treatment of the Squint That Occurs in the Upper Eye Corner.
This squint, which is called strabismus, may be either congenital or acquired. The acquired form results from injury or disease of the eye or similar conditions.
The method of treatment is to make the injury heal by separating the eyes and forming a membrane between them until it heals, and it is not advisable to use any substances that dry or contract in its treatment.
If you do this, the squint will return even more severely than before. Instead, use substances that soften such as honey and oil mixed with water, apply a paste made from cotton and bandage material dipped in grease and let it stay until it heals. Heal it with this.
Physicians should probe with all means except that they do not return to the original site, and this action which we have mentioned is one of the corrections for fistula, it does not return the location to its former state.
The fourth section.
Treatment of the fistula that is in the lower abdomen.
This fistula, which is below [in the lower abdomen], is in reality called a fistula and it is natural and it is linear. The linearity is due to injury or tear or something similar.
The method of working on it is to take a catgut and stitch it in the flesh and pass it from the left side to the right side until the thread becomes at the edge of the flesh, then move the flesh up with the catgut and cut it with a sharp knife.

Section Thirty.
On Extraction of Teeth.
It is necessary to treat the tooth from its ailment in every way, and it is possible for it not to be extracted if it has no reason to be extracted because it is noble until it is necessary to extract it.
If the cause for extraction of the tooth is firm, then it should be stabilized until the tooth heals. Often, the cause for pain is mistaken as being in the healthy tooth and it is extracted. However, the pain does not go away until the sick tooth is extracted. We have observed this behavior frequently from barbers (non-professional dentists).
If the pain in your tooth is clear, then it should be bound with a ligature around it using some force until the pus is released from all sides. Then move it gently with your fingers or soft tweezers until it aches.
Then, when the two large dogs are enabled, enable yourself well and place the ulna of the limb between your thighs so that it is immobilized and does not move. Then, draw the fracture in alignment so as not to break it. If it does not come out, take one of those tools and insert it under it from all sides with a hammer and chisel, moving it as you did initially.
If the fracture is impacted or collapsed, it should be filled with splinters and tightly packed with fine-grained plaster so that it does not burst when you tighten it with splints. It is necessary to compress it from all sides with the plaster.
Preserve your effort so as not to break it, some of which will return to the ulna from there, that is greater than the initial pain. Do not make what the unskilled blacksmiths do in the joints and approach the fracture without using what we have described.
Many people experience severe injuries where the fracture breaks and all or some of its roots remain. If a bone of the jaw is fractured as we have seen many times, then it swells afterwards due to drinking or eating salt and vinegar. If bleeding occurs from the site, it often happens that this is caused by applying pressure to the wound. In such a case, squeeze something made of gauze and apply it to the site.
If the forceps does not help you, use the delicate picture of the forceps that move the tooth first. It should have long handles and a short grip that is sturdy so it doesn't slip off when applying pressure on the tooth. This is the picture of large forceps.
The handles should be sturdy until it doesn't slip off when applying pressure on the tooth and doesn't break, while having short handles. It should be made of Indian iron or strong brass with smooth edges. On one side, there should be prongs that can fit together to grasp firmly and securely.
The handles should be designed like a lever, making them also strong for gripping.

The Third and Thirtieth Chapter.
To fix movable teeth, use threads of silver or gold.

The image of stitching is to take the thread and insert it between the correct teeth, then tighten the sides of the thread between the moving roots (one or more) until the stitch reaches the correct tooth from the other side.
Then return the stitch to the side it started from and tighten your grip gently so that the knot does not move, ensuring the knot is at the base of the roots to prevent slipping. Then cut the ends of the strong thread with scissors, gather them together and tie them tightly with a square knot, hiding them between the correct tooth and the moving tooth.
To prevent the loosening or breaking of the stitches, leave it as tightly knotted as possible. If it dissolves or breaks, re-tie it with another thread to ensure its longevity, and this is an image of teeth and their stitching in both correct and moving teeth, as you can see:.

The Sixth and Thirtieth Chapter.
In treatment of a scrotal abscess.
In abscesses occurring in the scrotum, there may appear nodules resembling those that appear externally, known as 'the two scrotal tumors.' If treated according to what has been mentioned in the classification, they will not recur.
If the abscess is hard like lead, with slight tenderness, do not treat it with iron. If its color is red and its substance thick, do not treat it with iron also, fearing bleeding. Rather, leave it until it heals; either pack it or let it burst from itself.
If it is white in color, soft and its substance is yielding, this is what should be excised. Before operating, one must ensure that the abscess has settled and its heat has subsided completely or partially.
When the patient is seated on a chair facing the sun, and his head is placed on a stone, open his mouth, take an assistant between your hands, hold his tongue down with this instrument (as shown in Figure).
Make an instrument from silver or copper, thin like a scalpel. When you press it with this instrument on the abscess and reveal it to your eyes, point a lancet at the tumor and draw it towards the outside without pulling any surrounding tissues.
Then it is to be cut with this instrument, its shape resembling a malleable leather, except that both sides of it are softened, each of them with a very sharp Indian steel or Damascene iron blade.
If this instrument is not present, then it should be cut with a lancet of such shape.
It should be cut with a sharp edge on one side and blunt on the other, first cutting one stone, then cutting the other of this type in its kind, then after cutting, it should be washed with cold water or vinegar and water.
If there is bleeding from it, wash it with water that has been boiled and made acidic by adding rattan splinters, or with vinegar and water, or something similar from the astringents until the bleeding stops, then treat it until it heals. If ulcers other than these two stones appear in the wound, they should be treated as described for the treatment of the stones, whether they are one or more.

The Seventh and Thirtieth Chapter.
On Cutting the Worm of Women.
If it is called 'Anbat' when it appears in the vagina and becomes swollen, it is white and elongated, then it is called 'Umud' if it is thick at the bottom and winding, otherwise it is called 'Anbat'. If it is treated as described in the section on treatment, there will be no cure.

The fortieth section.
To make from speech in the auricle of the abscess and break it.
The types of abscesses are numerous and they differ according to what is mentioned about them in this book, and they vary in their cavities and breaking points from two aspects, one of which is the type of abscess within itself and without any accumulation of fluids.
The second type is determined by the locations where it occurs in the body because the abscess that happens in the head is not the same as the abscess that happens in a joint, and the abscess that happens in a muscle location is not the same as the abscess that happens in a tendon sheath. A judgment on each of them is made regarding treatment.
Among the abscesses, there are some that should not be drained except after pus has formed in them and they have matured, and there are those that should be drained because they have failed to mature, such as abscesses that are near joints.
Because if an abscess occurs near a joint, the process may take a long time for the surrounding tissues to subside. It might cause damage to the tendons or the joint itself. Therefore, it may prolong the duration of that limb or the abscess may be close to a head.
If you delay squeezing the abscess until it has fully matured, you will injure that part (of the body) or be near the seat of the disease; squeeze it gently and it is necessary to squeeze the worm only when it is not completely matured so as not to cause the pus to flow into the wound. It will become a nasal abscess.
It will become difficult to heal, and it is necessary to learn the appropriate time for squeezing abscesses, which have matured when the worm's pain has subsided, pus has decreased, the redness has faded, and there are signs of maturity such as the hardening of the abscess's head and other indicators.
It is necessary to squeeze it from a lower position than the abscess if possible, as it will be easier for the pus to flow out towards a lower position or at a more prominent site of the abscess and with a stronger flow; the squeezing should move along the length of the body if the abscesses are in the hands or feet.
Positions of the muscles, joints, veins, nerves, and all flat areas without a particular prominence; if there is a prominence, the squeezing should follow that position; if the worm is in a muscular area, it is better to leave the abscess alone.
Until the boil is ripe, as we mentioned before, if you squeeze it before that, the fat of the fish will be long and abundant in sinews and cartilage, and possibly harden its eyes and skin, and some abscesses may burst on the surface of the body when necessary or according to what the limb needs.
Use a single lance for small abscesses and a wider one or multiple incisions according to the size of the abscess, and it may be necessary that some abscesses should not be closed and cut if it has become like a carbuncle.
It has become like something exposed in many graves and tombs, and from it a pustule forms with three corners, and from it a piece breaks off like the skin of an ox, as the scurvy of Arabs does.
Use the pointed lance for that which does not have a head, like the boils that are flat and swollen, and it is necessary to use the incisive lance or similar types of incisions if it does not have a head like the pustules that are raised, and if the abscess is large and has been for a long time and has been squeezed, it should not be pressed as all the pus will come out at that time.
He extracted some of it (the pus), then the abscess hardened for a day, then he extracted some more pus as well. This procedure is repeated gradually until all is evacuated.
If the patient is weak, a woman in labor or a child, an elderly person or a lunatic, the animal soul often does not withdraw with the evacuation of pus. Therefore, the patient may die without you noticing. Be extremely careful about this matter.
After puncturing these abscesses, it is necessary to clean the wound and examine it, if the abscess is small or if the wound is simple, use a linen cloth or wool from the cotton plant. If the abscess is large and the wounds are numerous.
It is necessary to insert a linen cloth or wool into each wound until they connect, and if the abscess has cut off a part of the skin or surrounded it, it is necessary to pack it with cotton or hemp not soaked and let it harden for three days.
Then, it is removed and treated with the appropriate remedies until it heals, if you see blood oozing during your procedure, use cold water and clay after drinking a mixture of powdered cotton and hold it on the wound several times.
If the discharge persists, it is necessary to use management, treatment, and medications as described in numerous sections of our book and its divisions. If you are during the cold season and the site of the abscess is abundant with coldness, it is necessary to apply heat by means of hot drinks and oil.
Place it [the medication] on the site, and if you are during the summer and the sites are warm, it is necessary to carry the remedies cooled by water or drinks and oil, all of this cold until the third day as we mentioned, it is necessary that the abscess be resolved and cleaned.
Apply what cures it until it has healed, for this is what is required in the treatment of abscesses. As for the methods of detailing each abscess, we have mentioned a brief summary for every abscess, its path to healing detailed.

Fifth and Forty-Fourth Chapter
On Breaking Types of Bones.
Bones have many types, and all their kinds have been mentioned in the classification. Here we shall explain the difference between bones and fractures, for a fracture is a problem. I say that a fracture will be accompanied by heat, swelling, and feared wounds until it heals completely. A fracture is complete when swelling and heat disappear, but a bone does not have heat, swelling, or wounds, and it has a special covering like a small box, which is its unique container. It will be on the color of the body, and its beginning is like a splinter, and it becomes like a boil and either large or small.
It is of two types, either it is festering or it contains moisture and the colors of moisture are numerous as mentioned in division. If you intend to treat the ailment, first probe and examine it with the instrument called the munds (Munds) as its image appears in the following chapter.
The size of the abscess, then bring out the munds and observe what comes out due to it. If moisture comes out, its color is known, break it open in a simple manner as mentioned for other abscesses. If no moisture comes out due to the munds, know that it is festering.
Break it open in a slanted manner with this appearance, as you are aware, and secure it with bandages and cut the skin from all sides with a scalpel while saving it if possible along with the ailment.
If the abscess bursts during the operation and you cannot extract it correctly, there is often no choice but to cut it off piece by piece until nothing remains of it. If something remains, either little or much, the ailment tends to recur more in this case.
If the wound becomes infected and some of its exudate remains, incise it around the edge with sharp instruments that are cutting, apply on top what drives away heat and worms, treat it with all possible remedies until it heals. If the disease is severe, make an incision in it and treat it with what is a strong remedy.
If the pulse becomes receding, either beating or not, and there is bleeding, the situation should be dressed with powdered alum and left for a day or two until the wound heals and stops bleeding. Then return to cutting what remains of the lesion.

Chapter 50.
On the worm that emerges from the bone.
As the worm appears in the ears and veins, similarly, the worm appears in the bone if it is hit or there is excessive fatigue or similar, and this occurs more in places of weakness such as joints and elbows.
In every place where there is movement, it is a worm that resembles the color of the body and is usually without pain. When pressed with great force, it feels like flesh (or muscle) but the worm is not gathered together in the depths of the body.
It is under the skin and moves in all directions without going forward or backward, so there should be no need to expose it with iron, as it may prolong time (healing). It should not be found in joints nor on the head or neck.
Make a small incision in the skin, if the worm is small grab it with forceps and cut it off at its root. If it is large, tie it with a ligature, cut it then remove it and close the wound with stitching until it bleeds.
Chapter One - Fifty-one.
In the section of cutting through arteries located in the abdomen.
Arteries called al-Futriyyah, similar to the vein (al-fatrah), are frequently found in the abdomen and other organs of some people. They have a slender base and a thick head, and can change into small vessels or become very large.
A man was observed with two growths in his abdomen, resembling the shapes of testicles but without any difference in color. His eyesight dimmed and they became swollen and leaked moisture constantly. I cut them both and weighed one around ten ounces and the other about six.
The work is to cut them, and if the cause is moist and the growths are white and soft at the core, then cut it with a broad knife and place the pieces in your hot coals so that much blood may gush out upon cutting.
If the bleeding persists, tie them with a wire of strong copper and leave it for a few days then tighten the wire again so that it does not loosen.
Every time a growth appears until it is cut and falls of its own accord, if the growth is hard at the core, then be careful when cutting it and do not hesitate, but know that it may not be in the abdomen, but rather in another part of the body. However, it can be partially or fully cut.
Then, cauterize to prevent recurrence, then treat until the wound heals completely. Be careful not to expose it to cutting through veins, as it will cause color change and dim sight, for it is a cancerous ulcer, and its mention of cancer will come later.
The second and fiftieth section.
In the treatment of anal warts.
Anal warts have many causes, either from the penetration of feces which exits from the rectum in other areas or from blood coming out of veins or arteries or from wind that inflames it.
If it is due to the penetration of feces and the exit of mucus, then the color of the wart will resemble that of the body and it will be pale without pain, and its appearance will vary. And if it is due to the exit of mucus, then its condition will vary greatly as described earlier. If you press it with your fingers, it may disappear temporarily and then return, often accompanied by itching and increased swelling upon entering the bathroom and extreme fatigue. If it is due to moisture, then it will be pale.
If you press it with your hand and it neither increases nor decreases in size, and if it was previously blood, then these are the signs of a tumor appearing black; but if it was previously meat, the tumor will be white and hard, remaining as such for a certain period.
If it was previously air, it appears clear upon pressing; work on this is to observe whether the secretion before it is blood from arteries or veins or air. In such a case, one should abstain from treatment as there is fear and danger, as you know in the chapter where I mentioned the tumors that occur due to arteries and veins.
If the secretion before it is pus or mucus, one should command the patient to hold himself and remain motionless for an extended period, then learn about the boundaries of the whole tumor. Then command him to lean back between your hands on its surface, then press with a broad hand around the tumor at the place you learned about the boundaries, then push the center of the tumor upwards with a large spoon, then bind the place of the press with strong thread or string, tightly and securely.
The suture of the ligature shall be tightened, then the middle of the abscess secured above the ligature will be opened and your thumb will enter it. If you find pus, the ligature will be loosened and the pus will be pushed inside the abdomen. If there is a wound, it will be closed with a suture.
Cut the protruding part, if it resists or bleeds, press on it and return to your work and take two strong threads, insert them into it. Threads will enter the incision made around the abscess, then tighten the abscess in four places using the threads.
If you wish to remove the thread and leave the area until the meat is healed and falls off by itself, or if it breaks and falls off, then treat it with what is necessary for healing until it is healed completely, if pus collects in the suture.
Or if there is moisture, it should be incised and the blood or moisture found in it should be drained, then treated with what heals the area.
Chapter Three and Fifty-Three.
Treatment of Cancer.
We have mentioned in the section of division, types of cancer and the way to treat them with medicines and warning against treatment with iron lest it cause harm, and we have mentioned cancer originating in the womb and warning against its treatment.
We have mentioned initially that when cancer is in a place where it can be entirely excised such as cancer in the arm or leg and similar limbs capable of removal, then it should be removed in its entirety. However, if it has progressed to a large extent, it is not advisable to approach it.
If I was unable to cure it, and no one before me has achieved it, and it reached that state, then work on it if we are able as previously mentioned, when it begins to ease the affliction, then proceed with it until it is in the veins full of pus.
Then the pus is set in a container that allows it to be worked on, then it is exposed to the cancer-eating substances that are suitable for it, and then it is encapsulated from all sides with the skin so as not to leave anything of its base. Leave the blood to flow and do not cut it quickly.
Apply pressure to the wounded area and extract all the coagulated blood with your hand or whatever tools you can, if resistance occurs in the operation, a large amount of blood will flow from cutting veins or arteries. Squeeze the artery until the blood stops flowing, then treat it with other remedies until it heals.
The Fourth and Fiftieth Chapter.

We have mentioned in the classification that there are various types of fractures and how water can gather, and signs for each type, as well as treatment with medicines. The one to be treated with iron is only the simple type (zqy) and no other type should be approached with iron; neither should the hollow type nor the cartilaginous type.
If that is the case, it means a battle, if you have treated this type of fracture with medicines and it did not work out, look carefully; if the cause is aging and weakness or if there is another disease other than the fracture like having a different illness.
Stretching or crushing and similar actions; if you find that the cause is not a disease other than the fracture, nor is it a child nor an old man, then perform the operation on it by locating the cause and standing between your hands. The servant presses his hand into the abdomen and forces the water downwards towards the vent. Then, he takes a curved hook on this figure:
He presses the hernia back towards the inguinal region and, with a thin, curved instrument (such as a hare's foot), he probes to see if it is a hernia from the side of the inguinal region.
The hernia should be pushed away from the navel by about three fingers below it, and if the hernia is due to liver disease, then the protrusion will be easy to push back with three fingers, but if it is due to an enlarged spleen, then the protrusion will be on the right side by about three fingers.
Moreover, the protrusion should not be on the side that the patient wishes to lie on, otherwise it may worsen by pushing the contents towards the weak position, then the skin is incised with a skin-cutter and the instrument is inserted into the protrusion and raised with the hand.
Grasp the hernia between skin and scrotum as if you are pinching it, and make an incision with the scalpel until the hernia reaches an empty place, which is the water place, then extract it and insert the instrument into the incision, this is its representation:
It is a resembling tube made of thin bamboo, which can be made from copper, brass or lead. It has a small hole at the bottom and three holes on its sides; two on one side and one on the other as you see.
The tip of it may be fitted with a stopper similar to the tip of a pen, as seen in this image.
On the upper end of the tube, there is a small slot. When the instrument reaches water, it will drain from the tube at a moderate rate so that you do not drain more than necessary in a given time. If you drain too much, the animal may die due to suffocation.
Or it may present with an obstruction close to death, but you should drain it according to its strength and what indicates this is the state of the animal in terms of its pulse and color. Then you remove the instrument and hold the water and this is because it holds the water for a certain period.
Due to the skin that blocks the hole in the needle that tells you to stop it on that state, then you return the instrument a day later if the animal appears likely for that.
Also from water, the vessel softens. This is done on certain days and you are vigilant about error until no more than the required amount remains in the water. If you hesitate with regards to the suspicious matter and leave something significant in the water, treat it by burying it in hot sand.
Much perspiration in the bath and exposure to the sun while enduring thirst, treating it with dried medicines until it subsides. He should be careful with the bladder and kidneys after removing the water as described previously.

If a wound is narrow, it should be treated with a probe repeatedly until it opens widely. As for those who have wounds not in their proper place, this happens when one of them is born with the wound at the end of the rectum and cannot evacuate feces.
Until the probe is lifted by hand above, and it has not been born before, the anus cannot reach the uterus in a stable manner. This is a very bad reason, and the method of work in this case is to draw the probe on its surface.

Keep in mind during your work to avoid bleeding, as it often occurs. For this, use something that stops the blood and treat the wound until it heals.
The sixth and thirty-fifth section.
On the boil that appears in the bladder, rectum, vagina, ulceration and the adhesion of the bladder to the rectum.
This ailment frequently occurs in dissection and it is called netou for fleshy tumors, it can be good or bad, the good one should be tied with a delicate snare.
Cut it until everything is clean, then place a swaddling cloth dipped in Egyptian mummy resin on it, and treat it later with Nakhla resin until it heals. If the tumor is bad and colored with pus, potter's clay should be used after cutting and grinding it.
If the tumor is in an ulcer that has not healed, and some of the tumors are inside the ulcer and some are outside, it should be removed first from the inside, until it drains. Then treat it from the outside.
Since when you treat them together, the ulcer is not secure from bursting, and it may also occur in females and ulcers with blackness and decay. It should be cauterized all that has turned black or is decayed.

If the bladder is consumed [with something] and its sack goes out at a time when it should be inserted into the male's urethra, it is necessary that tubes made of lead are inserted to drain the urine from it; as for the bladder being sealed with a covering.
This sealing only occurs in someone whose bladder was sound and had not been punctured, and it may be caused by injury or disease. In such a case, it is necessary to pierce the covering with a cannula until the bandage loosens and the bladder is relieved from all sides.
If the sealing is difficult to distinguish from a stricture, it is necessary to remove something from both the bladder and the covering because the covering is delicate and may be pierced quickly. Then, one should separate the covering from the bladder with a thin cane that has been soaked in cold water to prevent it from adhering again.

Chapter Seven and a Half.
On the purification of infants and the treatment of errors that may occur to them.
The cautery is not just any tool used in surgeries; when used intentionally and specifically for children, it should be performed skillfully.
The easiest way to achieve safety is by remembering the initial cautery, as it was not used in their practices and we are the ones who acquired it.
By experimentation, we found that most craftsmen and barbers use the cleaner with the mousse and the stick, they use the flame and the rope with thread and the cutting with the dagger, and I have tried all these methods.
I did not find a better method than the cleaning with the stick and the rope with thread, because the cleaning with the mousse often burns the skin as the upper layer of the skin is cut off while leaving the lower layer.
I was forced to cut further and the pain did not subside, and cleaning with the flame does not guarantee cutting the edge of the incision as it may enter the wound, and regarding cleaning with the dagger, the skin would likely tear apart or spoil the work, or the child's skin was short by nature.
Often, such are born who do not require purification and you have seen that. As for purification by the probe (cautery) and ligature with thread, experience has proven it to be effective because the probe above is like the probe below.
When you amputate your hand with the two blades in synchrony at a single time, the ligature thread will resemble a partition for the tendons from all sides and there will be no error in the joint, and it is better to deceive the child first.
It is not uncommon for one who understands little that you bind the thread in an amputation and let him go to a later time, then make him happy and keep it secret from him, so that you can do this with him and he will accept it without reason, then stop him between your hands at shoulder height.
A person should not sit and hold the probe (cautery) in his lap or under his foot, for the child's eye should not see the cauterization nor anything of the instruments. Then your hand enters into the amputation and you inflate the tendon and pull it up until the joint comes out.
Then clean what accumulates in it of pus, then bind the place with strong thread, then below that bind a second thread slightly, then take hold with your forceps and the suture needle at the lower bond firmly and cut between the threads. Then lift the skin quickly and extract the abscess, then let a little blood flow, for it is best and least painful for an abscess. Then clean it with damp pumice, then sprinkle on it from dry burnt lime or sand of the mill, for it is better, or powdered chalk, for it is also good.
Then lift the skin quickly and extract the abscess, then let a little blood flow, for it is best and least painful for an abscess. Then clean it with damp pumice, then sprinkle on it from dry burnt lime or sand of the mill, for it is better, or powdered chalk, for it is also good. Then place the abscesses on a pouch, and pack it with cooked egg whites boiled in water infused with barley flour, let it remain there for several days, then treat it with other treatments until it heals.
