"Chapter 49:
"On the drainage of varicose veins.
"This varicose vein is born in warm countries like Hijaz, Arab countries and other less cool desert regions where it may also appear in other parts of the body apart from the legs and it develops beneath the skin due to injury.
As discussed within living bodies and intestines, the process of quarq and the quarq that arises between skin and meat, a sign that this condition begins in the intestine is when there is severe burning in the anus, then the area swells, followed by the quarq beginning to emerge from the location of that swelling.
It appears to be the root of a plant or an animal. If any part of it emerges, it is necessary to apply a small piece of lead weighing between a dirhem and two dirhems, tie it up, and leave the lead attached to the anus.
Whenever something emerges from it to the outside, tie it in lead and leave it for a long time if possible. If it is very long, cut off part of it and tie the remaining and do not cut it from its root before all of it comes out because if you cut it, it will break, enter the flesh, and cause abscess, foulness, and painful ulceration in the area.
Therefore, it is necessary to gently dig and probe a little at a time until it comes out completely and nothing remains in the body. This quarq may come out from some people in lengths of five or ten fingers.
It has reached me that a man had a wound of twenty cubits, if it is cut for you at the time of your treatment, insert merodah in the hole and beat it with a long stick along with the body until everything within it releases. Try to dissolve the location with medicines for several days.
Treat the abscess with the treatment for boils, and this abscess may have many stalks and if it appears in the groin or on the leg itself, several openings may occur and pus will come out of each opening. Treat as described in the division [section] and according to what follows.
The Second and Forty-Ninth Section.
In the wound on the udar which is born under the breast and it is called udar abscess of the cow.
This disease is called udar abscess of the cow in some countries because it often affects cows and it is a small stalk that appears between the skin and meat, rises and descends in the body.
The pressure can be felt from one body part to another until it breaks where it did not break in the skin, and it becomes an abscess with some mixtures as it is susceptible to boils and animals and worms in the abdomen.
It is expected that when it (something) has been inflicted, if it swells in the body and rises to the head and reaches the eye, it may open there and come out, thus blinding the eye. This happens often, so if you wish to treat and remove it, it will be at its site and can be felt by touch.
To compress the area above and below it firmly, then squeeze it and remove it. If it is embedded in the flesh but cannot be found, apply fire to the spot until it burns away. Do not hesitate to increase the heat as much as expected for its destruction of the eye as we have said.
If you see it has become in the head near the eye, compress firmly below it on the eyebrow, then squeeze and remove it. The person who assisted should ensure thorough cleansing of the body with easy-to-blend ointments for the healing of the wound and preserve from food that causes inflammation.
Third and forty-ninth section.
In the incision on the sickness known as the Nafr.
This disease called Nafr in our land is a wound that appears in some limbs and then moves from one part to another, and you have observed what I describe to you.
Call to a woman who is lame in some of the plains, she revealed her arm and I blew gently into the vein of the arm, when an hour passed, you saw the breath moving along with the tendon as a pulse moves upwards most quickly like quicksilver.
If asked from place to place, the pain remained in that location and settled in the neck, then I sat for an hour and it spread throughout the body until it reached the other arm, then I cut towards where I saw it rotating the entire body.
I was amazed at the speed of its movement from one limb to another, and I had not seen this disease in this way before except that I saw a group of people suffering from pain that moved from limb to limb, but I did not see it with my own eyes as I did in this woman.
I was not able to do that except because the woman belonged to the Bedouins, whose bodies were exposed veins. From here, the moving breath became noticeable and it should not appear on this scale among those who specialize in healing and hidden moist bodies with concealed veins.
If you want to treat it and the owner of it feels pain, if its surface appears to you like we previously mentioned, then press upon it with a lancet and below it with a leech until that enclosed air is expelled and the place heals.
If you do not see it with your eyes, treat it by using the fat of the body and that which stops the flow of air and softens it, like camphor, cumin, and similar medicines.
The fourth and fortieth section.
On the extraction of thorns.
Thorns may differ according to their types and the parts of the body in which they are found, and as for their differences based on their types, some are large and small, some are pointed and others are blunt, and among them are those with three sides and those with four.
Among them, some have roots and others do not, and as for those that are in the organs according to their types, they may be on bones such as the skull, heart, liver, neck, kidneys, lungs, stomach, and other similar ones. If a thorn occurs in any of these organs and you notice signs of death that I have previously described for you, it is necessary to avoid extracting the thorn from it because death usually happens to its owner in most cases. When these bleeding signs do not appear and the pulse is not pulsating in the limb, extract it (the foreign body) and treat the wound, and among the symptoms of the skull are if it swells and bones protrude and the scalp that covers the skull is injured, it indicates a strong pain, swelling, and throbbing.
When these bleeding signs do not appear and the pulse is not pulsating in the limb, extract it (the foreign body) and treat the wound, and among the symptoms of the skull are if it swells and bones protrude and the scalp that covers the skull is injured, it indicates a strong pain, swelling, and throbbing. Redness in the eyes and tongue swelling, confusion, loss of speech or sound, and pus-like discharge from the wound site, it is similar to meat broth.
If these signs appear, refrain from treating the cause and extracting the foreign body unless it does not come out, and as for the symptoms of the heart if it occurs near the left side of the chest and you feel as though it has pierced something hard but not empty.
Perhaps the foreign body has movement similar to heartbeat and black blood is discharged from the wound, followed by coldness of the limbs and cold sweat, know that death is imminent, and a symptom of the foreign body is if the head is injured, white blood is discharged from the wound.
Incisions that are near the neck cause paralysis, change the color of the affected area and breathe heavily with high pitched breaths, requesting cold air to be blown, if there is a cough it will be close to small wounds and breathing will be very difficult along with severe pain.
All limbs move and if there is a cough, the same will happen with pain that is severe and blood comes out from the wound resembling liver in color, if it is the spleen that is injured it is unlikely for anything other than the spleen to come out from the wound.
If the abdomen is injured and gas escapes and something comes out from the wound or pus or rotten matter, there is no hope in treating it or removing the wound, if the wound is a bladder injury and urine comes out.
If something comes out from the wound and the pain increases on the affected area, it means death has occurred. As for the other limbs such as face, eyes, neck, chest, back, arms, legs, feet, and so forth, they will accept their fate.
If a wound does not cause bleeding or pain, and the wound is not poisoned, I inform you of some cases of similar wounds that can guide you in your treatment, one example being a wound on a man's face near his eye in the nose area.
I have extracted it from the other side, under the outer ear, and he was well. No harm occurred in his eye. I have also extracted a small horn that had happened to a Jew, which was located beneath his lower eyelid. The horn was curved and did not adhere except for its smaller end, which sticks to the bone.
The first horn was large, composed of four pieces of iron without ears, and the Jew was cured and no harm occurred in his eye. I have also extracted a small horn from a Christian's incision, and the horn was round.
He who had ears, I pierced between them and he was wounded in his incision, and I soothed him until I extracted it, and the Christian was cured. I also extracted a small horn from a man who had suffered it in his abdomen, and we expected that he would die from it.
When a period of thirty or so days had passed and nothing changed in his condition, I pierced the horn and it transformed into another form and I extracted it, and he was cured with no harm to him. I also saw a man with a horn on his back, so I made an incision on it.
After seven years, a tumor resembling a seed appeared in the root of a man's leg, and a woman was found to have a seed-like tumor in her abdomen. The tumor and the injury remained, but there was no change in her condition, and she found no harm in any of her natural actions.
You see another man with a tumor on his face and an injury, and there is not much pain for him, and similar cases are many. A seed-like tumor was removed from the nose of a man from the leaders of the state, as it had appeared in the middle of his left nostril slightly.
The tumor was completely removed, and it was advised to treat it after the tumor had appeared for three days. When I examined it with a fine probe, I did not feel anything and he found pain and swelling under his right ear due to the wound.
I hoped that the pain was from the tumor, so I pressed the area with a forceps with strong attraction and stimulated it, expecting it to twitch and show signs of the tumor, but there was no event in the area indicating that the tumor had reached the spot.
The patient has been bandaged for several days, but no event occurred; hence, it was sutured within that wound and the wound healer remained in a state of delay in healing due to its extraction. Afterward, I felt gravel inside his nose one day, so I informed him. Then, I placed a sharp medication (a purgative) on the wound for several days.
Until it opened and discharged, I felt a sharp edge of gravel adhering to the bone. Then, I enlarged the wound with that medication (a purgative) until a sharp edge of gravel appeared to us in the eyes, and he remained for about four months with it.
When the wound was enlarged and beetles were able to enter it, I drew them out with forceps, but they did not respond to my pulling; so I used gentle force without causing him any pain and applied various devices until I captured him one day with strong forceps according to their appearance in the last chapter.
The physicians used to rule that nasal congestion should not be compressed, but I compressed it and applied a snuff that was harmless and did not affect the bone, and I will inform you of the method for extracting some gravel so that this may serve as a measure and guide regarding what I have not mentioned.
The parts and details of this craft cannot be described or contained in a book. Only the skilled artisan, who measures much with little, can grasp what has not been mentioned and create new works and new tools when confronted by strange circumstances.
If you are cut from this craft, I say that the pieces come out of the limbs in two ways: either by pulling them out from the location where you entered or pushing them out from the opposite direction, coming out where they entered.
Either the splinter is located in a soft tissue, where it attracts pus and comes out spontaneously. In that case, you should not attempt to extract it until its surrounding tissue has relaxed, making it easier to pull it out. The same applies if it penetrates bone.
It is not necessary for you to exit (the abscess), leave it also for certain days and continue with drawing and moving it every day, as it will come out. If it is not necessary for you to make it come out after certain days, then pierce around the abscess in the same bone from all sides with a gentle probe until it spreads (the abscess), then draw it and remove it.
If the abscess is found in the bone of the head and it has settled within one of the cranial bones, and any of those symptoms which I have mentioned for you appear, refrain from drawing the abscess and leave it until the situation resolves after certain days.
Hold (the abscess) for drawing and removal, if it is very swollen and you are not able to draw it, use the probes around the abscess as described for you earlier, then treat the location until it heals. As for an abscess that has moved in the body. If the sensation is lost, probe it with a hook; if you feel it, draw it out with one of the devices suitable for doing so. If this cannot be done, make an incision and leave a wide wound, so that the swelling may recede and the wound not become infected, nor should it contain bone, muscle or nerve.
Make an incision on it until the wound widens and allows the pus to drain out. If there are any canals attached, remove the meat surrounding them from all sides using every possible method you can manage. If you cannot completely excise the meat, break the canals and open them up until the meat is freed.
If you attempt to drain the pus in any position, use probes directed towards all sides until it is freed and secure the tip of the probe so that the pus does not break and becomes difficult to draw out or extract, if this proves too hard for you at that time.
Leave it for the duration until the surrounding flesh has softened then resume treatment, as it becomes easier at this point; if you encounter bleeding, use the previously mentioned remedies for that, and preserve your efforts from cutting any nerve or muscle or vein and employ various methods.
You can extract the thorn in every direction, and it should be done with a probe and tweezers, as you have been described, and you must use a finger similar to the shape of the thorn when it was embedded for a better fit.
If you are unable to do that, then use what you can in terms of shapes, and as for the thorn which comes out from the opposite direction, it may either have been pushed out with something from outside or you may find one end of the thorn by touching the skin from above close by and see it protruding.
Break it open as wide as can accommodate the pliers, then draw it out, for it will facilitate its removal. If it has been grasped in a bone, apply pressure with your fingers until the thorn affects the bone and expands, then draw it out.
Leave it for as many days as it persists until it comes out, if the thorn has fallen off and you want to use a probe, introduce the straight instrument into the wound so that it penetrates the depth of the thorn, then apply pressure with it.
If the thorn is straight, apply pressure with an instrument that penetrates into its depth for it will facilitate its removal. If the thorn is poisonous, you must cauterize all the meat around it if possible, then treat it with whatever suits that purpose.
If the tumor is located in the chest, abdomen, diaphragm or flank and it can be approached with a probe and you are able to incise (it), then make an incision and save from cutting any artery or nerve and extract it.

The fifty-ninth chapter:.
On the ligature of arteries:.
The arteries that are commonly ligated in the body are thirty arteries, ten of which are located in the head. These include the two pulsating arteries behind the ears known as the carotids and the two arteries in the visible neck veins (carotid and jugular veins) and the two arteries in the eyelids known as the nasal arteries or "observers".
The vein in the middle of the forehead, the vein at the side of the nose, the two veins in the neck, the veins in the upper eye-sockets from the face, the veins in the lower eye-sockets, and these veins are known as the jugular; the veins under the tongue.
The veins which spread in the arm and hand are five, one of them is called the cephalic and it comes from the savage side, commonly known as the head vein or medial cubital vein, and it is a mixture of branches of the basilic and cephalic veins, commonly known as the body vein.
The basilic (also known as the inensal, commonly called body vein or thoracic vein) is located on the inside and it's also known as the saphenous vein. It is found on the calf and it connects to it and appears prominently above the ankle, namely the saphenous vein.
This is the artery that lies between the cuntisor and the piscisor, it has two branches. In the thigh and the leg there are three arteries, one of which is under the backbone from the wild side and the second is the scafin and its location is near the heel from the human side and the female artery and its location is near the elbow from the wild side.
In the other thigh there are also three arteries like it. As for the two arteries behind the ears, they should be cauterized and ligated, and the veins of the forehead that connect and branch off, including the temporal vein, the supraorbital vein, and the vein at the angle of the eye. The method of doing this is as follows.
It is to burn the top of the nose and char it in place of the arteries, then press down on the nose with a clamp until the arteries appear and their location behind the ears in the hollow places on the sides of the head are felt. Then you should probe them with your finger and find where the pulsations from the arteries can be felt under your finger. This is how it is taught.
Then take a curved knife, which is known as the scissors, and insert it under the artery in the skin until it reaches the bone. Then raise your hand with the artery and the skin above it and cut the artery together with the skin in a tight incision, and the length of the incision should be equal to two interlocked fingers.
Or take as much blood as desired, then squeeze them (the leeches) with the forceps and leave them until they escape, and if you wish to proceed immediately at the beginning of the book, cut and open them, and regarding the two veins in the temples, it is beneficial to tie them for headache, hard head, persistent nosebleed, and sharp pains directed towards the eyes.
And regarding the method of tying them, first feel for the pulse clearly on your finger and make a note of its location. Then raise the skin from above the pulse to the top with your index finger.
And insert the lancet into the vein from below and raise the pulse to above, then you will make a nick as you did in other pulses and draw blood according to your need, then press down firmly on the artery with your finger for one minute.
Then place a piece of cloth and bandage on it, press down on it firmly and leave it until it escapes, and if you wish to proceed immediately at the beginning of the book, cut and tie them as mentioned earlier, regarding tying the vein of the forehead, it is beneficial after tying the jugular vein for nosebleed, scrofula (tuberculous swelling of the neck), or erysipelas (a bacterial skin infection).

It is beneficial to excise it for the ulcer of the scrotum if it is due to hot blood, and its method is that you insert a hot iron into it and hasten it, pushing it from the root of the scrotum to above the navel with four fingers, with a thin, long forceps. It does not show otherwise.
If it appears, excise it in any condition, either by turning it (meaning twisting the wound) which is better, or by breaking it with a pumice stone or crushing it with forceps, for its location is safe and it is often hidden from people.
If it is not felt by touch, excise a part of its shaft, which is the one that appears on the surface of the foot around the ankle and toe, and keep it from nerves and send out blood of the desired amount.
Then, the wound is closed and a linen cloth is placed on the site of excision, and the site is tightened quickly, for it heals rapidly.
Chapter Sixty and Ninety.
On Suturing and its Application.
Sutures can be made from threads, wood, brass, or glass. Suturing with the condition of draining blood and without it.
This suturing without condition is done on two types.
The sutures for the ears are two sheets of the neck from both sides, the suture for the nose is below the lower jaw under the mouth, the sutures for the arms (kuffayn) are the shoulder, the sutures for the elbows ('assas) are at the elbow joint, the sutures for the legs (zendin) are in the middle of the arm pits, and the sutures for the ankles (saqin) and the sacrosciatic ligaments (arquobayn).
Suturing draws blood from the tense vessels in the meat, for this reason, it is not allowed to drop the power of constriction and suturing with fire or without it should not be done in any of the diseases that are related to obstruction until the body has completely evacuated.
If the need arises for suturing, whether from a patient or due to habit, we employ it at all times: in the beginning, middle, and end of the month, as well as anytime in between.
Some people find that they have an excess of blood which necessitates its removal by suturing. They may experience heaviness and pain in the head, and some may develop swelling on the face and head as well as the neck. Others might have ulcers on their faces or eyes, or suffer from blindness or cataracts, in which case they would require suturing.
Some people have excessive laughter, while others may find a taste of blood in their mouths and teeth grinding. Some may bleed excessively, have prolonged sleep, or see blood and redness during their dreams, as well as nightmares, surgeries, and similar phenomena. We have rarely seen anything like this.
In particular, it is our custom in the middle of the month to perform suturing after a lapse of two or three hours from noon, and as for stitching the wound, it relieves heaviness on the head and prevents fluid accumulation around the eyes.
But it should be done after the evacuation of the abdomen, and this incision may be a cause for the leakage of the cerebrospinal fluid. It is advisable not to use it if the patient has a cold brain or if there is a drop in it, as it will harm him greatly.
It is not advisable for the experienced practitioners to use it, and for those who have diseases in the brain, and for those who are subjected to it, may suffer from forgetfulness.
Therefore, the incision should be ordered to withdraw his hand slightly downwards, for fear of causing forgetfulness, and as for the incision in the neck, it is a cause for the leakage of bile and pus.
Therefore, it is beneficial to use narcotics and to restrict the soul, tighten the respirator, relax, and fill the chest. It is advisable to raise the incision in the neck slightly as if it descends, it will cause weakness in the heart and diaphragm.
And as for the incision of the temples, it is beneficial for treating wounds on the head, swelling, and fractures, and it is a cause for the leakage of pus. It is advisable that the incision is not too deep, so as not to cut the nerves, in case of bleeding.
As for suturing below the eyelid, it is beneficial for eye disorders and similar ailments in the eye, and a position can be assumed to remove a cataract that is in the eyes. And as for suturing of the chest, it is beneficial from the suckling cups which will be from milk supply and heat.
As for suturing the abdomen, it is beneficial to remove three arteries, al-basleeq, al-aakhil and al-qeefal because they attract blood from all the sharp arteries in the flesh, and those sharp arteries are attracted by another artery that is stronger than them until it reaches the three strong arteries.
It is necessary to command the suturer not to operate in a case where the location is visible and beneath it there are disorders and lesions, and as for a single suture that sews up an ulcer, it is beneficial from veins of the feet and vessels of the lower part.
It is necessary to command the suturer that the suture should be large and made of copper as the location requires a strong bandage, and perhaps the suture of glass may break and it depends greatly on conditions, and as for sutures for milk supply, it reduces the milk supply slightly.
Since it attracts blood from the entire body and is beneficial for abscesses in the kidneys, urinary bladder, and urethra, it cauterizes and is beneficial for boils and dimples, except that it harms the body greatly and causes poisoning in most people. The benefits of cauterizing the anus and rectum are close to the benefits of circumcision.
The method of placing the cautery is to place it first empty, and it should be held vertically and not too long. Then, you quickly place the cautery and quickly remove it so that the mixture can accept it evenly, without lingering. Repeat this and wait until the area turns red and opens.
The redness of the blood appeared, then it was necessary to press and repeatedly repeat the movement. If one of the people had meat that was torn apart in the wound, it was necessary to cauterize only once, lest it tear the area further.
The circumciser is ordered to widen the pressure and penetrate slightly, moving gently. If there was coagulated blood in it, it was necessary to press twice. In the first case, it should open a path for the gentle flow of blood and its water, and in the second, no extraction of the coagulated blood.
If the blood is very thick, it should be repeated thrice to reach its goal. If we want to remove a little blood, one condition will suffice. However, if we desire to remove much blood, our conditions increase, and if we are capable that the blood is thick.
It is necessary to set conditions deeply and the limit of the condition should be only the depth of the skin, it is not appropriate to use pliers or water when placing the clamp, nor anything that may harm the one being held. As for those whose skin is thick, hard, rough and tight.
It is necessary to lubricate the sites of the clamps with unguents that are smooth, soft and odorless. For example, if it is during summer, use oils like almond oil or benzoin oil or sweet almond oil or rose oil or pomegranate oil or oil of cinnamon.
If it is during the winter, use unguents like castor oil or sesame oil or camphor oil or juniper and similar. If the wound is cold and hard, use oils like mustard oil or linseed oil or poppy seed oil or soap nut oil.
If the wound is wide and the incision deep into the flesh, it is recommended to abstain from oil. Those affected should wash their wounds after suturing with warm water or cold water or with leek water or radish water or with linseed water or similar. As for those whose blood is excessively wet.
Wash the wounds with vinegar or camel urine and similar, and for those whose pus is thick, wash the wounds with sour milk or water of onion juice or leek water or similar. It is recommended to avoid suturing in the bath or near the bath.
Wait for an hour or two after leaving the bath and no one should sleep after suturing, it is not permissible to talk to the wounded person before or after suturing.
Take cold poultices such as leeches, hawksbill turtle shells, dried walnuts and almonds, skinks and similar, and make him eat fried garlic and veal kidneys, lamb stomachs and similar.
If a person is constipated, it is necessary to give him honey wine or mibatha or skenjabin azur and he should consume moderately aged perfumed vinegar which is between the old and the new, and he should be ordered to eat little food and his food should consist of fararij, qanabir, asafir and hamam's pigeons (white doves), and it is necessary that the drink on the day of surgery and evacuation be more than the food.
It is necessary to give some people tariq al-faruq or elixir of musk or shilthaa before surgery and evacuation, or after them, to strengthen the main organs, stimulate the blood and it should not be given to alcoholics.
The incisions without conditions are the ones that are made on the liver, spleen, lungs, abdomen, intestines, kidneys, and the rectum because these organs do not require any conditions, rather it is aimed at drawing blood from one organ to another.
We make an incision on the lungs in case of a pneumothorax or to release air from the organ because there is a pleural effusion in the organ, we make an incision on the abdomen and intestines as it relieves the organ and heats it and draws out the inflammation.
If a stone or gravel appears in the kidney, it can be drawn out by strong pulling, thereby opening the stone or extracting it from its place. Similarly, this is done if placed on the liver and spleen when wind gathers therein. These instruments are used empty, with nothing but oil.
The probe is heated or filled with boiling water for the extraction of bladder stones, and this is done by filling the instrument with hot water or water that has been cooked with certain herbs suitable for this purpose.
Then, the filled probe is placed at the location and held in place, then repeatedly applied according to necessity, and this is a photograph of the instrument used for extraction with fire:.

A flat plane, well-rounded so as not to harm the organ when placed upon it, and in its center there should be a stiff wire made of copper or iron where the bladder is heated with fire. This instrument can be large or small depending on the disease.
We shall employ them (cauterization instruments), for the ulcers of children and women are not those of men and adults; as for the manner of placing this cauterization in fire on the limb, it is to heat a filament of steel or a small piece of charcoal from a brazier and place it on the center of the suspended pole which is in the middle of the cauterization.
Make the ascent of fire almost below the cauterization to prevent burning the patient, then place it on the limb and finger on the hole we mentioned until we grasp the cauterization without causing pain, then remove the finger.
The boil comes out on that hole and the cauterization stays in place, then a filament is drawn along the edge and returned if necessary; as for the cauterization used in scrotal water disease, it has no suspended pole or hole.

The seventh and ninety-ninth section.
On the ligature (of veins).
The ulcer is mostly used in the majority of cases in the limbs that cannot accommodate sutures, either because of its small size like the eyelid and nose or because the limb is exposed to meat like fingers and nostrils and similar parts.
The method of using the ulcer should aim at obtaining pure distilled water from the pustules, then leaving it for a day and night in salty water until it ferments and nothing remains inside it. Then the body is emptied first by cupping or suturing, then the affected limb is cleaned.
Leave it to turn red, then put it on the affected area. If it adheres and falls off, that is better; otherwise, wash the spot with soap, then with plenty of water and salt, and squeeze it. If pus comes out after the ulcer falls off, that is a good sign. Dip a piece of cedar wood in cold water.
Place it from above until the artery is severed, if blood flows abundantly, pour on it a powder or a piece of cotton or similar items from the cauterizing irons until the bleeding stops or apply tourniquets to the place of incision.
Leave it until the ligature adheres to the place, for the blood will stop flowing. If it is necessary to reapply the ligature, do not use that ligature again unless there is no other option; if you cannot avoid using the same ligature, clean the site with pig's blood.
Insert a probe into the wound until something from the blood emerges, then place it [the probe]. If it feels something of the blood adhering to it, let it remain at the site; if you want to remove it, sprinkle something from ashes or salt or charcoal on it, and it will fall off onto the site.
Third Chapter.
On algebra.
This chapter is also relevant to the craft of medicine and deals with fracture algebra, a term used for analyzing the angles formed by fractured bones.
Be aware, my sons, that this chapter may be considered foolish by physicians and the common people; those who have not even read a book on medicine or understood a single letter of it.
For this art, the science has become famous in our country without any fault of my penmanship. I have benefited from it as much as my reading of the early books allowed me and I have endeavored to understand them, until I extracted that knowledge from them. Then I insisted on practice and training for the length of my life.
I have drawn for you in this chapter all that is covered by the knowledge. I have experimented with it after approaching it for you, refined it from the long-winded and shortened it to its essence, made it clear to the highest degree, and illustrated for you in it many images of the machines that are used in it.
It is an addition to the explanation as you did in the preceding chapters, and there is no power except by Allah the Exalted.
The first section.
In it, the fundamentals of breaking bones and their presentation are gathered together before we begin to mention the broken and dislocated parts one by one. Therefore, in this chapter, it is necessary to summarize the discourse and outline its sections. It is essential for you to understand and remain steadfast on the truth that you and those who are eager to learn this noble craft are not alike.
It should be done immediately when something breaks or dislocates or fractures or falls in; first to locate it, or to reduce it, or both of them at once. Nor should anything prevent from doing so, like weakness of strength, or the one that happened to it was a child or an old man, or the time is very hot or very cold.
Then he should restrict his diet to cold foods like bird's meat and mutton, avoid alcohol and tough meats, abstain from overeating, and let every food fill the veins with blood until the wound is safe and there is no fear of infection by any material into the place.
Then the cause should return to its original management, if the broken bone is set in plaster, the patient should eat foods that strengthen much and nourishing, which contains pairs like barley and wheat and beans and pulses and corn meal of cow or goat. And egg, lean meat, strong drink and suchlike, for this management makes the setting of the fracture quicker and better; and know that broken bones in men who are vigorous or old cannot be joined and united back to their original nature forever.
Fractured bones become soft and brittle, and the fragments may connect or interlock. However, nature causes a layer similar to callus on all sides of the broken bone. But, it is stronger than the original bone and can resist pressure until it heals completely by joining with each other.
They connect until they reach maximum strength and hardness, just like before, so that nothing can harm them.
Therefore, it is necessary to provide the patient with food containing nourishment and energy, as well as building materials, as we said earlier. It should be noted that fractures can vary in type depending on the affected bone because a fracture of the hand bone differs from a fracture of the skull, and a fracture of the rib differs from a fracture of the backbone.
Similarly, each and every bone is different from the others. We will discuss each type of fracture separately, and it is possible that the type of bone fracture can also differ within itself.
Because it may be a crushing fracture without the occurrence of fragments, or a fracture along the length of the bone with fragments and broken pieces in it, or a fracture accompanied by injury to the skin and wound, or a simple clean fracture.
For each type of fracture, there is a specific method in setting it where its description will be detailed at its place, and what is known as bone fracture is characterized by swelling, displacement, appearance for feeling, trembling when you touch it with your hand.
If there is no swelling, trembling or feeling of bone when touched with pain and the cause is not apparent and there is no discomfort, it is not a fracture but it may be a sprain or a simple fracture here or a strain, in which case it should not be moved or probed.
But carry medicines that will be mentioned later when the place conforms, then press it gently but firmly, and know that if bone is crushed and displaced without any protrusion, except for fragments, then all parts have separated from their owner.
It is necessary for you to proceed to set and align it before it develops a hot swelling, for if a hot swelling occurs, leave it for days until the hot swelling subsides, then align it in any way you are able using forceps or other method.
Know that the dislocation and its reduction is easier than a bone which has fractured, then pressure shall be applied on what will be described afterwards. If there is a bone with fractures within it, it is necessary to divide the limb from both sides, whether it is an arm or a leg.
If the limb is small, tie it with two ropes or hold it with a rope and hand; position your limb in its natural position until the broken parts of the bone extend. Then form a reduction by placing the ropes in their respective positions from all sides as much as you can manage with pliers and forceps.
Strive not to cause the patient pain, harm, or distress by your efforts, and strive to fix one of the bones with its partner in the best possible position. At this time, touch and press them both with your hand if you see anything unusual there; correct and reduce it within your ability.
Be aware of severe pressure and excessive force, as many ignorant people often cause this and frequently produce heat or swelling in the limb as you have observed from their actions repeatedly.
Then, after setting and securing it, he should keep that limb immobile and quiet, warning not to move it during his wakefulness and sleep, and in case of change or agitation, and upon any sign of swelling. All movements should be aimed at stretching and extending it, and it should be allowed to regain its position as long as the pain persists.
In case the limb is set with pain or discomfort, it should not be moved from its position to another where there is no pain, but rather it should be allowed to remain in that position as long as there is no further pain or discomfort.
To prevent any joint problems when setting a broken limb, know that the nature and size of broken bones varies. Those which are smaller such as fingers, toes, or tendons should be set in the following manner:... (The rest of the text is about the specific method for setting small bones)
For fractures in the long bones such as arms, legs or chest, it is necessary that the bones be aligned straight because the wide ligament requires a large bone and provides firm immobilization from all sides without any gap.

Know that not every fractured bone needs to be set with the jaws from the first day, and this is because if the bone is large, it is not advisable to place the jaws on it except after five or seven days, or more, depending on your safety from developing a hot fever.

A second type of dressing is for the treatment of hot inflammation and the draining of wounds, specifically. The second dressing exerts force on a broken bone. This dressing is made by pounding together bayberry leaves and paper from the khashkhash tree, then moistening them with water. The shortened dressing is used for setting a fractured bone.
The remedy for a wound is made from the root of the castor-oil plant, beebread, poppy seeds and crushed barley. All are ground together until they form a paste. If the limb is not broken, it should be applied as is. If the limb is broken, it can be mixed with water or water of kuzbara instead.

The quirkot is made from lard and oil, and it should be of a moderate consistency between hardness and softness. Then apply the warm wool bandage soaked in oil or lard onto it, tie it up overnight until the hot inflammation calms down and the swelling subsides, then return it to the delicate pressure and soft padding, do not tighten it with your initial force.
Then allow it to heal, if you see that the inflammation, redness, pain, swelling and all symptoms have completely subsided and have returned to the soft padding and gentle pressure, then return it as you initially did. If nothing abnormal happens in the limb, leave it as it is.

Leave the limb in warm water every time you remove the plaster, and let it be done every three days and reduce the pressure slightly; with this action the nourishment will reach the limb and it will heal quickly. As for what the ignorant do among the forced ones in fracturing the limb again.
If [the surgeon] does not initially press where it should be pressed and then presses on a swelling, this is an error committed by them and a grave mistake. Even if it were correct to mention it in their books, no evidence of its effect can be seen from any of them in this matter - the cauterization. The correct action is not to perform it [cauterization].
The second section.
On the fracture at right angles in the head.
Types and shapes of right-angled fractures in the head are numerous, their causes varied, and their origins complex. The fracture may be due to a sword blow or it may be that the bone is broken all the way down to the scull beneath the bone. As when splitting wood.
And therefore this type of fracture is called a splitting fracture, or it may be a sword cut through some bone but not all the way through and it is called a simple fracture in general. The injury caused by these two types of fractures may be severe or minor.
The fracture may be a simple or compound one, and its cause is a blow with a stone or falling on a stone or similar circumstances. This fracture can either be an opening one which penetrates the soft tissue beneath the bone, or it can occur on the face of the bone.
These fractures may also be either large or small, and one type of fracture can occur hidden within the bone in the scalp area and is a simple, easy break.
This type of fracture is called "hairline" because it can occur due to a fall or strike with a stone and enter the bone surface from the outside, leaving a shallow indentation as if exposed to corrosion by copper when struck, part of which enters into the inner area.
It is mostly found in the soft bones of the skull, such as those of children. These fractures can be simple or compound, and we will discuss their treatment in their respective sections. All these types of fractures are identified through examination.
They are examined using probes and the removal of rotten flesh from them, and as for the hairline fracture, it is recognized by palpation of the bone, rubbing and pressing on it, because the fracture appears black. As for the treatment of the fracture, first consider the symptoms of the injury.
If you see symptoms that indicate fear, such as sweating, shaking, fainting, loss of intellect, voice loss, shyness, sharp crying, eye bulging and reddening, or similar symptoms, do not approach the patient or treat him. For in most cases, death occurs with these symptoms. There is no remedy.
If you see symptoms that indicate safety, then treat him. This is because if the injured person comes to you immediately after being wounded, and this was in the cold days.
It is necessary to try to remove the bone before the tenth day in all cases, even if it is in the summer. However, it is necessary to hurry up in removing the bone before the seventh day before what lies under the bone can be spoiled and these symptoms described occur.
If the bone is broken and has reached the spoiled marrow on the skull and there is bleeding and swelling, then it is necessary to cut the damaged part that I have described for you, which is to shave the head of the injured person.
Uncover the bone from any side that will enable you and according to the shape of the injury and whatever does not harm the patient. If during the uncovering of the bone, bleeding or hot pus occurs, counteract it as necessary.
The place should be filled with crushed myrobalan [a type of mangosteen] mixed in wine, oil, and lard, and the wound massaged until the worm settles and the discharge is secure. Then, the bone will be reinforced and extracted, and this procedure can be performed on either one of two aspects of the work.
One aspect is to cut the bone with a fine, tight sawblade. The appearance of this [cut] is as follows:.
